  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6e299c36-9d89-42fc-8556-5b2e450a49ba'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText13297151623724294793" style="display:none">For months Clara Gardner trained to face the fire from her visions, but she wasn't prepared for the choice she had to make that day. And in the aftermath, she discovered that nothing about being part angel is as straightforward as she thought.<br /><br />Now, torn between her love for Tucker and her complicated feelings about the roles she and Christian seem destined to play in a world that is both dangerous and beautiful, Clara struggles with a shocking revelation: Someone she loves will die in a matter of months. With her future uncertain, the only thing Clara knows for sure is that the fire was just the beginning.<br /><br />In this compelling sequel to <em>Unearthly</em>, Cynthia Hand captures the joy of first love, the anguish of loss, and the confusion of becoming who you are.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_12165008').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_12165008').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_12165008').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16806784785242283686">**<b>Our Cynthia Hand Interview</b>, where she addresses many of the questions that arise from this series is <a href='http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/01/epic-cynthia-hand-interview-part-one.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> and <a href='http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/01/epic-cynthia-hand-interview-part-two.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>. Enjoy!**<br/><br/>There aren't words enough to express how gorgeous this book is. Fans of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly__1_' title='Unearthly (Unearthly #1) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unearthly</a> who might have worried whether Cynthia Hand could deliver a second installment that would do justice to the story need worry no longer. This sequel lives up to and exceeds every expectation I had for it, and I only wish I could hand this book to every single would-be author who is even c</span>
  <span id="freeText16806784785242283686" style="display:none">**<b>Our Cynthia Hand Interview</b>, where she addresses many of the questions that arise from this series is <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/01/epic-cynthia-hand-interview-part-one.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> and <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/01/epic-cynthia-hand-interview-part-two.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>. Enjoy!**<br /><br />There aren't words enough to express how gorgeous this book is. Fans of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly__1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> who might have worried whether Cynthia Hand could deliver a second installment that would do justice to the story need worry no longer. This sequel lives up to and exceeds every expectation I had for it, and I only wish I could hand this book to every single would-be author who is even considering writing a YA paranormal romance. Because this is the template for what every teen romance/sophomore/angel book should aspire to be.<br /><br />As the story opens, Clara is still recovering from the fire in which she went against her "purpose" as a part-angel in order to follow her heart. Her brother Jeffrey is still acting strange, Angela is helping Clara to test her powers, and eventually, we are introduced to an important congregation of angels and learn more about their purpose on earth. Best of all, we get some fabulous time with Tucker as he and Clara further enjoy what has to be one of the sweetest and truest young adult romances ever put to page. I could not stop smiling as I was reading the story, because their relationship is just so warm and happy and perfect. I love that, in the middle of all of Clara's bigger-than-life abilities and problems, she and Tucker still have such an amazing time together doing such blessedly normal and human things.<br /><br />We all knew what was coming next, though, right? Christian was such an attractive enigma throughout so much of the first book that I was really hoping we'd get to know him better in this one. And while I dreaded the thought of this turning into a horrible love triangle situation that would devastate everyone while dishonoring them as well, I hoped against hope that the author would handle this tricky situation with as much honesty and grace as possible. And boy, did she ever come through. I am a huge fan of Tucker's, but Cynthia Hand somehow does the impossible and shows us how the flicker of friendship between Christian and Clara grows incrementally stronger everyday. By the end of the book, he has shown himself to be a rock-steady, understanding, and <i>fun</i> presence in Clara's life <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[not to mention an incredibly hot one :D  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and it's pretty near impossible not to fall in love with him in a pretty deep and meaningful way as well.<br /><br />This book made me so very happy in so many ways, and there are unbelievably beautiful angel moments in it, with descriptions of gorgeous feathered wings, flying, and luminous "glory" that are just marvelous. I've always appreciated the wry honesty and warmth with which the relationship between Clara and her mother was written, and here we discover so much more about her as a mother, as an angel, and as a <i>person</i> in a way that is incredibly touching. Clara learns a great deal about her family and about herself in this novel, and her deepening strength and maturity combined with her funny, sensitive narrative only made me love her further. I also enjoyed the distinctly outdoorsy feel of the mountains in this book, the presence of many of the adults, and the nuanced portrayal of the bad guy, as well as the thoughtfully considered mentions of angel lore, religion, and references to <i>Paradise Lost</i>. Oh--and big, big bonus points for a prom scene that didn't make me want to do violence!<br /><br />But this book also broke my heart in more ways than one. There is an exquisite tenderness to this story that I never could have imagined, and while I think some elements of it may upset some fans, I hope readers will go into it with an open mind and an open heart. I had many theories and opinions and hopes going into it, and I can honestly say that coming out of it, all of that has changed--and I am firmly convinced that it is for the better. I am tremendously moved and inspired by this story, and it's a testament to Cynthia Hand's pitch-perfect writing that we are so gently eased into new realizations and growth in a way that feels so right and so emotionally true. <br /><br />My heart was aching when I turned the last page. But it was also overflowing with love and deep appreciation for the splendid journey that I didn't even know I wanted to go on. After reading a second fantastic YA book from this author, I have absolute faith in Cynthia Hand, and I am so looking forward to seeing where she will take us next.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2011/11/hallowed-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br />P.S. I am dying to discuss the specifics of what happens in this book in the comments below, so please, tell me what you think of where this story went in spoiler tags! I can't keep this to myself any longer. Please be aware that the spoilers tagged in the comments are REAL, so please don't click if you haven't read the book yet! But the spoilers in the review are all in good fun, and safe to click. ;)<br /><br />Also, a spoiler for people who were worried about Midas the horse in the last book: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They're still looking for him in the beginning of this one. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16806784785242283686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_166797536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166797536" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166797536?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Unearthly</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      Me!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=left-me-in-a-sad-emotional-state">left-me-in-a-sad-emotional-state</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=gimme-gimme-gimme">gimme-gimme-gimme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=deserves-every-one-of-those-stars">deserves-every-one-of-those-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=didn-t-disappoint">didn-t-disappoint</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-need-it-like-a-fat-kid-needs-cake">i-need-it-like-a-fat-kid-needs-cake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=cried-my-eyes-out">cried-my-eyes-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=oh-yeah-baby">oh-yeah-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166797536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10990308748159406217"><br/><b>Hallowed is out! I can't wait to re-read it!</b><br/><br/>Oh, Cynthia Hand, how could you do this to me? I feel like this book should come with at least a warning. Something along the lines of:<br/><br/><b>WARNING: This book may cause readers massive amounts of fangirling/fanboying. Do not be alarmed if you encounter symptoms of swooning, emotional instability, and immediate depression after reading. </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349593ra/703544.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yeah...cause that's exactly what happened to me. Many of you may remember that I expressed in my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160254253' rel='nofollow noopener'><i>Unearthly</i> review</a> how I was</span>
  <span id="freeText10990308748159406217" style="display:none"><br><b>Hallowed is out! I can't wait to re-read it!</b><br><br>Oh, Cynthia Hand, how could you do this to me? I feel like this book should come with at least a warning. Something along the lines of:<br><br><b>WARNING: This book may cause readers massive amounts of fangirling/fanboying. Do not be alarmed if you encounter symptoms of swooning, emotional instability, and immediate depression after reading. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349593ra/703544.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yeah...cause that's exactly what happened to me. Many of you may remember that I expressed in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160254253" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Unearthly</i> review</a> how I was initially reluctant to read this series. Angel PRN books seem to be the worst of the worst in YA literature. So you can imagine my happiness when I come across this gem of a series. If there were ever a reason needed as to why I voted for Cynthia Hand's <i>Unearthly</i> as Best Young Adult Fantasy &amp; Science Fiction, it would be <i>Hallowed</i>. If you were thinking that Hand couldn't do it again, you were wrong! <br><br>First off let get this off my chest because it's seriously bothering me:<br><br><i>"This beautifully woven tale will appeal to fans of Lauren Kate, Becca Fitzpatrick, and Aprilynne Pike."</i><br><br>Excuse me while I hurl. Are you <b>kidding</b> me? Stop it. Please. Do not lump this series in with those sorry books. <i>Hallowed</i>, for starters, has a plot. The characters have real depth. The love interests aren't trying to <b>kill</b> Clara. What it should have said was: <i>"For fans of real YA PNR literature."</i> *Breathes* Okay. /end mini rant.<br><br>I think it goes without say that I loved this book. I stayed up past 4am to finish this it. Once again, I could not have predicted the outcome! There are so many plot twists and mysteries revealed and it's not what you would expect at all. And I have a sinking feeling that <i>Hallowed</i> is sure to upset quite a few fans...<br><br>If you think I'm going to sit here and feed you spoilers, sorry kids, not gonna happen. However, I can tell you some of the things I LOVED about <i>Hallowed</i>:<br><br><b>The character development</b><br>Fans will be happy to know that we do indeed find out more about Christian, Clara's mom, Angela, Jeffery's purpose and last, but certainly not least, Tucker Avery. *Cues the swooning*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380347026ra/701356.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Clara's mother definitely sees more development. And at first I found myself really irritated with her for keeping secrets, but by the end of the book, I couldn't bring myself to be angry at her any longer. We were left with so many unanswered questions at the end of <i>Unearthly</i>, mostly thanks to Clara's mom, but rest assured, many are answered. And of course, with more answers we get even more questions. <br><br><b>The love triangle</b><br>I'm sure you saw that coming, as did I, but here's the thing: I liked it. I usually hate love triangles because I find them a bit played out and predictable. But it <i>worked</i> so well in <i>Hallowed</i>. This probably has something to do with the fact that Hand wrote these characters so well. Their relationships are very believable and heartbreakingly realistic. We see a whole other side to Christian and Tucker. It's rather easy to love them both because they both care deeply for Clara and respect her. There are no semi-abusive love interests here. How about that? ;)<br><br><b>The prose, the pacing, and the plot</b><br>I never thought I could come to love the use of present tense prose, but I felt it was so perfect. We are really able to connect with Clara on another level because of that, especially everything that she goes through in this book. And she goes through <i>a lot</i>. The simple sentences and Clara's ramblings really helped me feel everything Clara felt. The pacing was a bit slower in this book than the last, but again, it works so perfectly. Hand gives us the opportunity to let it really sink in. The pacing just goes hand in hand with the plot, which too is very subtle. At first you become eager to get to the end, but you will come to dread it. So beautifully written.<br><br><b>The dialog</b><br>Cynthia Hand, you are so slick and I love you for it. Those Twilight burns you put in there? Oh, yeah, I think you know how brilliantly awesome that was. <blockquote>
  <i>Before I moved here, I never got the whole love-triangle thing. You know, in movies or romance novels or whatnot, where there’s one chick that all the guys are drooling over, even though you can’t see anything particularly special about her. But oh, no, they both must have her. And she’s like, oh dear, however will I choose? William is so sensitive, he understands me, he swept me off my feet, oh misery, blubber, blubber, but how can I go on living without Rafe and his devil-may-care ways and his dark and only-a-little-abusive love? Upchuck.</i>
</blockquote> Yup, that's pure win right there. <br><br><b>The ending</b><br>It was so heartbreaking. Clara just didn't get a break in this book and I felt for her so much. I just wanted to hug her. And at the end I felt like <b>I</b> needed a hug. Hand, you had me crying at 4am! I can't believe you <i>went</i> there in this book!! I mean, seriously, I was having a fit over here:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349593ra/703545.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Shock: "I.CAN'T.EVEN."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349593ra/703546.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Disbelief: "NOOOOO!! She did not just do that! NOOOO!"</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380349593ra/703547.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Depression: "How will I survive until 2013? I'm doomed. Doomed, I tell ya."</i><br><br>Cynthia Hand tore my heart out and made me eat it...<br><br>...<i>and I liked it...</i><br><br>P.S. I recently found out <a href="http://www.deadline.com/2011/10/csi-showrunner-carol-mendelsohn-sets-up-slew-of-drama-projects/" rel="nofollow noopener">there might be a TV show based on <i>Unearthly</i></a>.<br><br>Ummm, Hollywood? Let's get this one right, m'kay?<br><br><i>An ARC was provided by the publisher. But this in no way swayed my views on this book.</i><br><br>Like this review? Well, what are you waiting for?! Come visit my blog <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10990308748159406217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_230504279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230504279" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230504279?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=book-schizophrenia">book-schizophrenia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-ought-to-love-but-dont">books-i-ought-to-love-but-dont</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=what-the-eff">what-the-eff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=disappointed-me">disappointed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=mixed-vibes">mixed-vibes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230504279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6473423964043204434">I hate love triangles. More than anything else in fiction, I really, really, <b>REALLY</b> hate love triangles. More than the stalking and the insta-love and fragile, insecure, yet perfect heroines. I mean, at least with most insta-love couples, once they're in love, they STAY in love. <br/><br/>So anyway, it's not that much of a surprise that Hallowed sort of killed my happy Unearthly-buzz. This book was nothing like what I expected it to be, and I can only rue the change. Cynthia Hand did an amazing, wonderful</span>
  <span id="freeText6473423964043204434" style="display:none">I hate love triangles. More than anything else in fiction, I really, really, <b>REALLY</b> hate love triangles. More than the stalking and the insta-love and fragile, insecure, yet perfect heroines. I mean, at least with most insta-love couples, once they're in love, they STAY in love. <br /><br />So anyway, it's not that much of a surprise that Hallowed sort of killed my happy Unearthly-buzz. This book was nothing like what I expected it to be, and I can only rue the change. Cynthia Hand did an amazing, wonderful thing with Unearthly, and somehow, it feels like she <i>undid</i> all of that work with Hallowed. That said, though, if I DO have to read about love triangles, this was one of the better-handled ones.<br /><br />I reread Unearthly before I started on Hallowed, and I was struck anew by how much I enjoyed the book. The writing was simple but real, with occasional flashes of humor and the sort of likeability that only deepens with a second read. And more importantly, despite being a very relationship-focused story, it did have a plot and a certain amount of character growth and action. Hallowed feels less like a complete book in and of itself and more like a long-drawn out episode on daytime television. <i>"My life is a soap opera,"</i> Clara says, and it turns out to be all too true. <br /><br />Here's the reason why Hallowed disappointed me so much, I want to cry. Most YA paranormals push the idea of a soulmate, that one person who's just so perfect for you, you feel like you want to die if you can't be with him. The connection is so strong, and perfect, but you know what, it's not <i>real</i>. And it's this idea that Clara fights back against, in Unearthly, and she does it beautifully. She falls in love, for real, with someone who's hot, but not picture perfect, someone whom she actually knows- she makes the <i>choice</i> to fall in love with Tucker and I think that's the reason that little book resonated so strongly with so many of us. It wasn't some fated, pre-destined epic love, but something so warm and achingly sweet, we all wanted to be seventeen and in love again. <br /><br />Not so much Hallowed. Yes, sure, Clara still fights her "attraction" to Christian, feeling that she is more than a pawn in some supernatural game, but it feels more like she's fighting an inevitable current, like the choice she made was worth nothing, because she is being pushed back to the place she tried so hard to escape from, and if that's the case, what's the point in that, really? <br /><br />As for Christian, I'm still not seeing the attraction. I mean, sure, we find out more about him, his life, his circumstances, but at the end of the day, he's still that YA sap, the beautiful-looking, perfect one who's willing to sit for hours under some girl's roof waiting for her to give him time of the day. In Hand's world, he's an anomaly. He never seems quite as real a all the other people, the ones for whom the world is NOT well lost for love. <br /><br />And so much of this book was just angst of various sorts. Some it was understandable. For example, I really, felt Clara's pain <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when she realizes that her mom is close to death. Books like The Goddess Test could really take a few tips from the simple, yet moving way in which the death of Clara's mom was handled, the peaceful passing followed by the hope of a better afterlife, and the numb disbelief of those who are left behind.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But I felt like the spotlight focused so heavily on Clara, and her internalizing of every emotion she felt, her thoughts, her motivations, her struggle against all the changes in her life, that pretty much everything else in the book took a backseat. The connection I felt between Clara and Tucker in the first book never manifested itself in the second. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think I would have sympathized a little more with Clara's struggle to choose if I had ever felt like she gave her relationship with Tucker a fair chance. From the very beginning of this book, there is a sense of doom hanging around this relationship; if Clara loved Tucker as much as she says she does, why doesn't she fight harder? She never confronts Christian, or makes him go away in any real sense. See, there is a big difference between telling someone to get the hell out of your life because you're in love with someone else, and passively ignoring them while they spend a gazillion hours outside your window, playing the noble guy.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And don't even get me started on Jeffrey and Angela and Wendy. Who are these people? I thought I knew them back in Unearthly, but they don't get so much as a cameo in Hallowed. Angela had this whole cool, creepy vibe going in the first book, but she's no more than an accessory in the second, and not a very interesting one at that. Jeffrey, of course, drops a bombshell on us at the very end, one that really had me sitting up and paying attention, but for most of the book he's just this sullen shadow that Clara pays a bare minimum of attention to. I think the thing that annoyed me most with Clara in this book is how very <i>helpless</i> she turns out to be. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So Angela tells her she's seen Clara at Stanford in her vision, and Clara just <i>accepts</i> it? No doubts, no fighting her destiny, just acceptance? And the way she never really makes a push to find out what's eating Jeffrey? This is not the girl I thought I knew.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And Wendy might as well have not been in the book for all the role she plays. Disappointing, disappointing, disappointing. <br /><br />I'm not saying this is a bad book, because it's really not. Cynthia Hand has a great hand (get it?!) with characterization, and as usual her closing chapter is beautiful and leaves you longing for more. The thing is, I had higher expectations for this book, I wanted it to be strong and fierce and unique, and it fell far, far short of that mark. I will be reading the third book, and any books that come after that, but if Hand fails to recapture the magic of Unearthly, I for one, am going to a very unhappy camper. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6473423964043204434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200891459" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200891459?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405259927" href="/book/show/12165008-hallowed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200891459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13393486092092182409"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I am going to have to sadly admit that this series is not my cup of tea. I tried to like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_' title='Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unearthly</a> after reading all the rave reviews but found it only okay, it didn't blow my mind like I was so sure it would. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_' title='Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hallowed</a> was even less appealing to me, I read three chapters and even that was a struggle - but now I do think I'm starting to see why. I think if I happened to meet Clara in real life, let's just say she enrolled at my university, we would be friendly to one another, perhaps mumble a</span>
  <span id="freeText13393486092092182409" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I am going to have to sadly admit that this series is not my cup of tea. I tried to like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly___1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly, #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> after reading all the rave reviews but found it only okay, it didn't blow my mind like I was so sure it would. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a> was even less appealing to me, I read three chapters and even that was a struggle - but now I do think I'm starting to see why. I think if I happened to meet Clara in real life, let's just say she enrolled at my university, we would be friendly to one another, perhaps mumble a polite greeting when we passed in the corridor but I don't think we would ever be close friends. We have so little in common. Clara is, in many ways, the girl I have never been... nor really wish to be either (though, I would like to be able to fly).<br><br><b>(1)</b> Clara is the kind of girl who will have relationships filled with sweet romance, hand-holding and utter tameness. I appreciate that this is a young adult novel and I didn't exactly expect graphic sex scenes - or, in fact, any sex at all - but "Tucker still has this notion that since I have angel blood in my veins he should try to keep my <i>honor</i> in tact" is practically Victorian repression.<br><br><b>(2)</b> Clara cannot even admit to herself that she has the hots for Christian as well as Tucker. She dreams, daydreams and thinks an awful lot about the guy but "no, no, Tucker is my future". Who is she kidding? It's not like every reader doesn't know already that there's a whole love triangle thing going on... so why is our heroine being stupid? <br><br><b>(3)</b> I read three chapters. In these chapters, apart from a quick recap of what happened in the first book, we spend all the time in the middle of Clara's daydreams of marriage and babies. Or experiencing kissing Tucker through Clara's mind, which is naturally out of this world, sensational, practically orgasm-inducing... or seeing visions of Christian, which is just <i>bad, bad, bad</i>.<br><br><b>(4)</b> And why oh why did this book get so biblical? Three chapters, I must remind you, and I don't know how many times I heard about god and the bible. Look, my religious beliefs aside, everyone is fully entitled to believe what the hell they want - but that doesn't mean I want to hear it about it in chapter two. And a lot.<br><br>I could read the rest of the story but I can tell we are not destined to love one another. And that's okay, right now I have so many other things to read. To anyone who is put off by my lack of chemistry with this book, navigate towards <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/165648951" rel="nofollow noopener">Wendy's</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137488827" rel="nofollow noopener">Tatiana's</a> review to see how it worked out for people who "got" Clara more than I did.<br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_137488827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137488827" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137488827?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=romancelandia">romancelandia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137488827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1736780260050287843">3.5 stars<br/><br/>It's a relief to know I won't regret all the hyping of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly__1_' title='Unearthly (Unearthly #1) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unearthly</a> I've done over the last year. Even though I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_' title='Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hallowed</a> less than its predecessor, the series is still going strong the way I see it. <br/><br/>Whatever was praiseworthy in the 1st book remains so in the 2nd - the teen romances are still healthy (I won't even bash the inevitable love triangle - it is written well enough; it is not perfect, but not unbearably annoying either), the heroines are strong and the heroes are kind and re</span>
  <span id="freeText1736780260050287843" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />It's a relief to know I won't regret all the hyping of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly__1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> I've done over the last year. Even though I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a> less than its predecessor, the series is still going strong the way I see it. <br /><br />Whatever was praiseworthy in the 1st book remains so in the 2nd - the teen romances are still healthy (I won't even bash the inevitable love triangle - it is written well enough; it is not perfect, but not unbearably annoying either), the heroines are strong and the heroes are kind and respectful, the angel lore, while more Hell- and Heaven-heavy this time, still doesn't cross the line into preaching. There is also an added bonus of a meditation on free will vs. destiny which I find quite interesting, especially within a genre as soulmate-ridden as PNR. <br /><br />But there are things that didn't fully work for me. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a> is a sad, sad book. In addition to Clara's anxiety over her failure to fulfill her purpose at the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly__1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a>, she starts having more visions, this time predicting the death of someone close to her. Plus, the new, strange connection with Christian muddles things with Tucker. Complications are all around Clara.<br /><br />If <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7488244.Unearthly__Unearthly__1_" title="Unearthly (Unearthly #1) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Unearthly</a> was a sweet PNR, its sequel is about death and grief. The glumness and occasional drudgery of it was pretty intense for me. Some lightness in the beginning would have made for a better reading experience, building up to a more emotional impact in the end and a bigger climax, which, frankly, was virtually non-existent in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11563110.Hallowed__Unearthly___2_" title="Hallowed (Unearthly, #2) by Cynthia Hand" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallowed</a>. <br /><br />I am concerned about the concept of purpose as well. Will it all come together eventually? The way Clara's purpose appears to come back and back again, I am afraid the series has an option of becoming a never-ending stream of books, all focusing on a purpose which so far looks exclusively romance-related (just today I read on the author's <a href="http://cynthiahandbooks.com/q-a.php" rel="nofollow noopener">website</a> that there might be more than 3 books in, what I originally thought, was a trilogy). That would be boring to me.<br /><br />I will still be reading the 3rd book when it comes out in 2013. Fingers crossed, the series does not get prolonged beyond 3 books and the last one packs some interesting surprises and revelations while untangling the plot that at this point looks a tad convoluted. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1736780260050287843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16696434577841300968">A review of this is now available on <a href='http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/03/review-hallowed-by-cynthia-hand.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog</a> as well! Check it out.<br/><br/>____________________<br/><br/>Wow, I....<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/260589.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ms. Hand, what have you done to me?<br/><br/>This book was such an emotional roller coaster, I can't even tell you.<br/><br/>Clara. Clara's honestly one of the YA heroines that I really love. She's just so... I don't know, there's something about her that just makes me love her. When she complains about something, it never annoys me. I kind of sympathize with her, you know? There's just that likable-ness in her that I c</span>
  <span id="freeText16696434577841300968" style="display:none">A review of this is now available on <a href="http://wildheartbookblogs.blogspot.com/2012/03/review-hallowed-by-cynthia-hand.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> as well! Check it out.<br><br>____________________<br><br>Wow, I....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/260589.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ms. Hand, what have you done to me?<br><br>This book was such an emotional roller coaster, I can't even tell you.<br><br>Clara. Clara's honestly one of the YA heroines that I really love. She's just so... I don't know, there's something about her that just makes me love her. When she complains about something, it never annoys me. I kind of sympathize with her, you know? There's just that likable-ness in her that I can't really explain very well. And besides:<br><br><p>“Before I moved here, I never got the whole love-triangle thing. You know, in movies or romance novels or whatnot, where there’s one chick that all the guys are drooling over, even though you can’t see anything particularly special about her. But oh, no, they both must have her. And she’s like, oh dear, however will I choose? William is so sensitive, he understands me, he swept me off my feet, oh misery, blubber, blubber, but how can I go on living without Rafe and his devil-may-care ways and his dark and only-a-little-abusive love? Upchuck.”</p><br><br>How could I <i>not</i> love her after saying that?<br><br>Anyhow, let us move on to Tucker and Christian... Oh boy.<br><br>In my review of book one, I stated that Christian was a mere obstacle to me, and that my heart belonged completely, 1000% to Tucker. But in this book, Cynthia Hand made both these guys completely irresistable. I cannot deny that Christian swept me off my feet in this book. I both love and hate Hand for being able to do that. I love it because that's incredible to me, to make both guys in a love triangle absolutely amazing. I hate it because choosing between them will be very hard to do. She made me question my faithfulness to Team Tucker.<br><br>Why can't we make a team Tustian? Or Chriscker or whatever. ._. Because I love them both. Choosing just one of them is impossible. ;_;<br><br>But yeah, I can't think of anything else to say that won't spoil the book, but I will say that waiting for book three is physically painful. I'm not kidding.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/481713.gif" height="200" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_230285728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230285728" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230285728?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230285728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12105535159123959874"><i>*This galley was provided to me by the publishers via netgalley.</i><br/><br/>This review can also be found on my blog, <a href='http://cuddlebuggery.blogspot.com/2011/11/review-for-hallowed.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cuddlebuggery</a><br/><br/><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Hallowed is a difficult book to rate because it's not going to appeal to everyone. If you're the kind of person who needs fast paced adventure then you're better off picking up something else. Hallowed is very much focused on relationships, self-growth and destiny.<br/><br/>It continues its themes with purpose, faith and trust - these themes are extended here and well constructed</span>
  <span id="freeText12105535159123959874" style="display:none"><i>*This galley was provided to me by the publishers via netgalley.</i><br /><br />This review can also be found on my blog, <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.blogspot.com/2011/11/review-for-hallowed.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a><br /><br /><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />Hallowed is a difficult book to rate because it's not going to appeal to everyone. If you're the kind of person who needs fast paced adventure then you're better off picking up something else. Hallowed is very much focused on relationships, self-growth and destiny.<br /><br />It continues its themes with purpose, faith and trust - these themes are extended here and well constructed. <br /><br />Clara is awaiting the return of the Black Wing and dealing with her newfound relationship with Tucker whilst Christian is in the background being all sexy and mysterious.<br /><br />Struggling with how her purpose ended up last book, she is losing faith in herself and distrusting her family.<br /><br />I felt like the strong characters and great writing by Hand really carried this novel because otherwise it might struggle very strongly from middle book syndrome. The plot is not progressed a whole deal but there are a number of big revelations. <br /><br />But what Hand does bring to it is a great amount of self-awareness and just enough awkward reality and relationships to pull it through. I liked this book better than the first one and I felt like the writing was just a little tighter and stronger in this one.<br /><br />Over all, a good, solid second installment from Hand and I look forward to the next.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12105535159123959874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8595759894306167513">My gosh. What an outstanding sequel. This broke my heart :'(& kept me captivated, also, swoon. Full review to come.<br/><br/>Review: <br/><br/>When HarperCollins released Hallowed on netgalley, it seemed all my reading buddies stopped whatever they were reading and charged straight into book two. After Unearthly was so universally loved (by hard core critics, fans of YA paranormal and non-fans of YA paranormal, aka: me) Hallowed was an insanely anticipated released. <br/><br/>Guys, it delivers. <br/><br/>It is a compelling and unputdo</span>
  <span id="freeText8595759894306167513" style="display:none">My gosh. What an outstanding sequel. This broke my heart :'(&amp; kept me captivated, also, swoon. Full review to come.<br><br>Review: <br><br>When HarperCollins released Hallowed on netgalley, it seemed all my reading buddies stopped whatever they were reading and charged straight into book two. After Unearthly was so universally loved (by hard core critics, fans of YA paranormal and non-fans of YA paranormal, aka: me) Hallowed was an insanely anticipated released. <br><br>Guys, it delivers. <br><br>It is a compelling and unputdownable read that evokes a whole gamut of emotions. <br><br>For me, it was the complete package as far as reading experiences go: <br>I read it in a single day, absorbed and hopeful. <br>I swooned (plenty more gorgeous kissing scenes). <br>I felt for the characters (as a whole, Hallowed is a sad, sombre kind of book that induces an achey feeling...). <br>I LOVED the love triangle, which feels true and complicated, achey and not sensationalised at all. <br>I particularly love Christian in this installment. Tucker is still awesome as well.<br>I still love Clara’s voice. She sounds so teenagery without ever falling into overly-done YA snark. She’s moody and funny and sad and ever-so-likeable (if clueless at times ;)).<br><br>There may be some things I am still unsure about (the angel mythology and the whole rules around purpose). I missed seeing more of Wendy. I am wondering why Jeffrey feels like such a loose canon ball and no seems to notice (?). It drove me CRAZY how Clara’s mum was never straight up with her about some of the mysteries of all the angel stuff. Some of the twists seemed inevitable to me, but that was cool. But all of these ponderings didn't detract from my enjoyment AT ALL. I seriously LOVED reading it.<br><br>For a second book, there is no slump. It rolls straight on from Unearthly and sets up book number two for Clara’s next adventures: heading off to college (yay for heading into new adult territory!). I really cannot wait to follow the characters on and see what is in store for them, hey. <br><br>If you haven’t read Unearthly yet (!) now is the time to get on board. Hallowed will be out in Australia on January 1 (although last year, HarperCollins released Unearthly early, making it available for Christmas ~ so keep an eye out!) and in the US January 17. <br><br>Hallowed has my golden, shining seal of approval. The Unearthly series is fast becoming a fave of mine and I SO recommend them to all fans of YA ~ and any teens you know (it’s a breezy, engaging read).<br><br><br><i> Thanks to HarperCollins and Netgalley! </i><br><br>Aussie cover for HALLOWED revealed:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356391i/708041.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Isn't it gorgeous? very eerie and atmospheric.<br>alongside our cover for UNEARTHLY:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380356391i/708042.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thanks for the heads-up, Braiden :)</span>

<div id="review_139255610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139255610" />
    <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-"><img alt="Jillian -always aspiring-" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393566262p2/3085436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139255610?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jillian -always aspiring-" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jillian -always aspiring-" href="/user/show/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-">Jillian -always aspiring-</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who wants to read a good series about angels, heaven, and hell</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-couples">best-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=best-endings">best-endings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=heroines-i-love-and-or-admire">heroines-i-love-and-or-admire</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=wowed-me">wowed-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=worth-every-star">worth-every-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=forewent-sleep-to-read-it">forewent-sleep-to-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3085436-jillian--always-aspiring-?shelf=world-building-worth-noting">world-building-worth-noting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139255610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15107897093735620476">Oh, Cynthia...you must have taken your kid gloves off after <i>Unearthly</i> since you really managed to deliver a beating with <i>Hallowed</i>! If a plot twist wasn't clubbing me in the head, the emotions of the characters were punching me in the stomach! The experience left me feeling rather drained and a bit bruised...but it was worth it.<br/><br/>Clara Gardner, an angel-blood by birth, thought that her heavenly purpose had died away with the last embers of a wildfire...but she is far from done with visions telling </span>
  <span id="freeText15107897093735620476" style="display:none">Oh, Cynthia...you must have taken your kid gloves off after <i>Unearthly</i> since you really managed to deliver a beating with <i>Hallowed</i>! If a plot twist wasn't clubbing me in the head, the emotions of the characters were punching me in the stomach! The experience left me feeling rather drained and a bit bruised...but it was worth it.<br /><br />Clara Gardner, an angel-blood by birth, thought that her heavenly purpose had died away with the last embers of a wildfire...but she is far from done with visions telling of things to come and actions she may have no choice but to take. When a recurring dream hints at the funeral of someone close to her, she hastens to find answers of who, when, where, and why -- even as she must contend with her feelings for two vastly different boys who represent two very different choices and futures.<br /><br />Much like its predecessor, <i>Hallowed</i> was a pleasant surprise to me: not only did it continue its subversion of many of the common tropes to be found in young adult paranormal romances, but it also managed to avoid the trap of the "sequel slump" (where the second book in a series feels more like filler than a necessary story). Even with "the dreaded love triangle of doom" present front and center in this installment, the characters never act in ways that are inconceivable, intolerable, or completely irrational. Rather, they all seem to be just handling their lots in life the best ways they can: "coping" eventually becomes the default mode for many of them.<br /><br />The story here is much more focused on Clara's growth as a character than I had been expecting. With all the revelations and discoveries, they all seem to add layers to her character to the point that no longer does she resemble that starry-eyed angel girl of <i>Unearthly</i>'s beginning, who was so intent on fulfilling her purpose and glad to do so. Clara has grown up. She has seen the gray and experienced sorrow and grief, and now she looks at her purpose as more of a burden rather than a joyous occurrence. Clara's struggle with free will and "destiny" is one of the best conflicts to the series, even as it becomes clear that destiny means that many things cannot be avoided.<br /><br />And that's part of my problem with <i>Hallowed</i>: the angel-bloods can take as many winding roads as they want, but eventually all of them will find themselves fulfilling the stages of their purposes in some fashion. It may take more time, they may fight against it, but "destiny" will happen. Honestly, I don't know how I feel about that, especially since the "big picture" of Clara's purpose has yet to be revealed.<br /><br />I also have another problem: Christian, the enigma and constant presence in many of Clara's purpose-centric visions. Christian is the mysterious boy who has the answers but hides them, who uses kindness and compassion as a way to subtly manipulate the heroine, and who seems to have more of an agenda than he's saying: basically, he's not much better than the typical YA paranormal love interest, at least not from what has been presented of his character in these first two installments. Though Christian is presented in a much better (and, dare I say it, more deceptive) package, I can't help but look at him with distrustful eyes, and I almost want to call him an antagonist waiting to happen. But the doubt in me says, "No, the subversions in the series will only go so far. Don't expect too much. You'll only be disappointed if you do."<br /><br />Doubts aside, I do have hope that Cynthia Hand will continue to subvert this convoluted paranormal genre young adult literature has had on its hands for the past few years. I have hope that she will keep surprising me with her story's twists and turns, that all my worries and resignations are needless, that by the end I'll change all my ratings for the books to five stars because of how blown away I felt by the entire scope of the story once it was revealed to me. But I have to wait and see if that day will come. The <i>Unearthly</i> series has one or two books left and much more story left to tell...so I'll wait and hope.<br /><br />Regardless of my own qualms, I highly recommend <i>Hallowed</i> because it represents the kind of storytelling and characterization that many YA books are sorely lacking. If you like young adult paranormal books and have yet to read <i>Unearthly</i>, then you're missing out, so make sure to pick up both <i>Unearthly</i> and this sequel in the near future. You may just find yourself enthralled by a story you had never even hoped to expect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15107897093735620476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_231430010" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231430010" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231430010?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231430010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5448684735519294236">I had a whole bunch of worried speculations going into this book: a whole bunch of thoughts like, “if this happens…then I’m out.” And they basically all came true. But she made me like it.<br/><br/>How did she do that?<br/><br/>I’m still not quite sure. Even now, I can think of several problems that I have with this book, and yet; my major feeling upon reaching the last page was, “that was pretty good.” <br/><br/>And I find myself right back here, in the place where I am filled with worried speculation…this time for book thr</span>
  <span id="freeText5448684735519294236" style="display:none">I had a whole bunch of worried speculations going into this book: a whole bunch of thoughts like, “if this happens…then I’m out.” And they basically all came true. But she made me like it.<br /><br />How did she do that?<br /><br />I’m still not quite sure. Even now, I can think of several problems that I have with this book, and yet; my major feeling upon reaching the last page was, “that was pretty good.” <br /><br />And I find myself right back here, in the place where I am filled with worried speculation…this time for book three. I’m chiefly worried because, even after two complete books, I have no idea what she’s trying to say. There’s something here about faith and free will vs. destiny, but I’ll be damned if I know what it is. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So…they have free will? But apparently when they choose to use it, and not follow the visions/dreams, bad shit happens. Her mom tried to exercise her free will and look what happened! It felt like years of punishment! Until she finally gave in. As a free-will loving human, that kind of makes me recoil, more than a little bit. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Even after two books, I’m still almost completely in the dark about the mythology, the rules, the world I’m inhabiting. I don’t know which way is up or which side is evil or what the hell a <i>purpose</i> is truly all about.<br /><br />The main character is not helpful in this regard, either. She’s for the most part placid, unquestioning, and even seems in denial. When she finally starts to uncover the right questions, she seems to forget them before they’ve even been asked. It’s frustrating. And I think that I would be okay with her placidity if I felt that it was a true representation of her character, but unfortunately, it feels more like a device to stall the progression of the story. I hate feeling manipulated like that.<br /><br />Jeffrey’s whole story line just doesn’t make any sense to me at all. For all that Clara’s mom seems to be present, attentive, and strict with <i>Clara</i>, she seems to be completely oblivious when it comes to Jeffrey. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And then he runs away just in time for Clara to go off to college. Problem solved! Also, why wouldn’t Jeffrey tell anyone about his purpose? He seems to have absolutely no reason to keep it a secret. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The romance surprised me. I didn’t roll my eyes or cringe. So many of my YA romance pet peeves are here, but she writes it in such an honest way; it’s hard not to feel for everyone involved. I’ve never been one of those people who get really invested in team A or team B though. In fact, and this will be shocking to the literary nerd-girls out there (ie, all of you), I really was not that upset when Jo rejected Laurie and then married middle-aged Professor Bhaer. I know. Settle down, ladies. If it feels right, I can go with it.<br /><br />However, I am so caught up in the free will vs. destiny aspect of the romance. This next part will be a completely random tangent so feel free to skip it.<br /><br />Once, one of my more blunt friends asked me, “Do you love your kids more than your husband?”<br /><br />And I didn’t even have to think about that for a second before saying, “Yes.” The love that I have for my children is so completely ingrained and uncontrollable and primal. I know without a doubt that I would commit violence or sacrifice myself just to keep them safe. I have no choice in this, and I don’t want one.<br /><br />But the love that I have for my husband is something that I choose. It’s something that I have to keep choosing every single day. I have to work to keep it burning, to keep it new. And I think that’s what makes it so powerful and so wonderful. I could let it fade and stagnate, could let it grow stale, but I don’t. Because it’s something that I <i>choose</i>. It’s something that I <i>want.</i><br /><br />So when these destined, soul mate romances come up in fiction, I always have a hard time. I will always root for the love that’s chosen, because I think that part of what makes romantic love real is the fighting for it.<br /><br />I will probably read book three, because I still want to know how everything is explained. Here are my crazy predictions for book three:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />1)	Angela and Christian are half-siblings.<br />2)	Angela’s “boyfriend” is a dark wing, who she tried to lure and question (Possibly her own father? Ick.).<br />3)	Some of the other 75%-ers will show up. <br />4)	Angela will majorly over-think her mission and will learn a valuable lesson about her ability to choose. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Michelle Branch – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=NERmgwWfnoI&amp;ob=av2e" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodbye to You</a><br /><br />Because the romance in this book is so angsty and teenagery but somehow I still liked it. This one is for Clara :(<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5448684735519294236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_140768563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140768563" />
    <a title="Sandy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy"><img alt="Sandy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1320017147p2/4515165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140768563?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandy" href="/user/show/4515165-sandy">Sandy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=chemistry-sigh">chemistry-sigh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=favorite-character">favorite-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=can-t-stop-thinking-about">can-t-stop-thinking-about</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=premise-i-love">premise-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=settings-i-love">settings-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4515165-sandy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140768563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4444897669446360779">This series is what every other angel book wishes it could grow up to be.<br/><br/><i>Hallowed</i> is "middle book" at its very best.<br/><br/>Out of all the paranormal creatures in YA, angels get by far the worst treatment. Three of the worst YA series all feature angels, and until <i>Unearthly</i>, I thought perhaps it was impossible to write a decent angel book. But <i>Unearthly</i> was not decent--IT WAS AMAZING. That delicious, slow-build romance between Clara and Tucker. A strong, likeable heroine with a realistic voice. A vivid,</span>
  <span id="freeText4444897669446360779" style="display:none">This series is what every other angel book wishes it could grow up to be.<br /><br /><i>Hallowed</i> is "middle book" at its very best.<br /><br />Out of all the paranormal creatures in YA, angels get by far the worst treatment. Three of the worst YA series all feature angels, and until <i>Unearthly</i>, I thought perhaps it was impossible to write a decent angel book. But <i>Unearthly</i> was not decent--IT WAS AMAZING. That delicious, slow-build romance between Clara and Tucker. A strong, likeable heroine with a realistic voice. A vivid, gorgeous setting. Intriguing mythology that makes sense. Tucker. (Did I mention Tucker?) Ever since I closed the pages of <i>Unearthly</i>, I've been clamoring for a sequel.<br /><br />In Cynthia Hand's follow-up novel, she DELIVERS. She makes me feel things about characters that I never thought I could. She takes this in the direction hinted at throughout <i>Unearthly</i>, but she makes it work (in ways this Team Tucker girl didn't think were possible) and adds some complexity with other unexpected twists. My heart was aching--ACHING--when I finished this book.<br /><br />Cynthia Hand, how did you make me like Christian? I'm as TEAM TUCKER as they come, and yet you drew me in to see Christian's goodness and charm and caring with such a sly hand. I'm no advocate of love triangles, but this one is as good as they come.<br /><br />And the writing? As addictive and snappy and heart-breaking as ever. I love that Cynthia can poke fun at her own book and genre with funny little lines about stalker girlfriends and love triangles and jealous boyfriends. Her writing makes these characters feel REAL, so real that she can make me feel absolute joy and then devastation because of the struggles and choices these characters face. And trust me...you will feel a gamut of emotions reading this.<br /><br />Cynthia Hand has shown that <i>Unearthly</i> was no fluke. This woman can WRITE. This series shines with stellar characterization, fascinating mythology, compelling choices, and Tucker (it needed to be said). I cannot wait to see what she has in store next for these beloved characters.<br /><br /> P.S. Jackson Hole and Idaho, I love you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4444897669446360779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
